The classification header has already been emitted. Do NOT emit it again. This skill handles **execution only** for STANDARD and STRICT tier tasks.\n>\n> If for any reason no classification header was emitted before this skill was invoked, emit one now using ONLY the tier values STRICT, STANDARD, LIGHT, or EXEMPT (no other values are valid).\n\n# /sc:task-unified - Unified Task Execution with Compliance\n\n## Purpose\n\nUnified command that merges orchestration capabilities with MCP compliance enforcement. Automatically classifies tasks into compliance tiers and enforces appropriate verification.\n\n**Key Benefits**:\n- Single command replaces confusion between `sc:task` and `sc:task-mcp`\n- Automatic tier classification with confidence scoring\n- Appropriate verification for each task type\n- Prevents over-engineering for trivial changes\n- Ensures safety for critical changes\n\n## Triggers\n\nUse `/sc:task` when:\n- Task involves code modifications with downstream impacts\n- Complexity score >0.6 with code modifications\n- Multi-file scope (>2 estimated affected files)\n- Security domain paths detected (auth/, security/, crypto/)\n- Refactoring or system-wide changes requested\n\n**Auto-Suggest Keywords**:\n- High confidence: \"implement feature\", \"refactor system\", \"fix security\", \"add authentication\", \"update database schema\"\n- Moderate confidence: \"add new\", \"create component\", \"update service\", \"modify API\"\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\n/sc:task [description]                           # Auto-detect all dimensions\n/sc:task [description] --compliance strict       # Force STRICT tier\n/sc:task [description] --compliance light        # Force LIGHT tier\n/sc:task [description] --skip-compliance         # Bypass compliance (escape hatch)\n/sc:task [description] --verify auto             # Auto-select verification\n```\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\n### 0. Classification (Already Performed)\n\nClassification was handled by the `/sc:task` command before this skill was invoked. The tier has been determined and the classification header has been emitted. Proceed directly to execution based on the classified tier.\n\n**Reference** — the tier keyword tables (for context only, do not re-classify):\n- **STRICT**: security, authentication, database, migration, refactor, breaking change, encrypt, token, session, oauth\n- **EXEMPT**: explain, search, commit, push, plan, discuss, brainstorm\n- **LIGHT**: typo, comment, whitespace, lint, docstring, formatting, minor\n- **STANDARD**: implement, add, create, update, fix, build, modify, change (default)\n\n### 2. Confidence Display (Human-Readable)\n\nAfter the mandatory classification header, show a human-readable summary:\n\n```\n**Tier: STANDARD** [████████░░] 80%\n\nClassified as STANDARD:\n- Keywords matched: add, implement\n- Confidence score: 0.78\n- Considered alternatives: STRICT (0.35)\n```\n\nIf confidence <70%, add prompt: \"⚠️ Low confidence. Override with: `--compliance [strict|standard|light|exempt]`\"\n\n**Note**: The machine-readable header (Section 0) is for telemetry/A/B testing. This human-readable display is for user understanding.\n\n### 3. Execution Phase\n\nExecute task according to tier requirements:\n\n**STRICT Execution**:\n1. Activate project (mcp__serena__activate_project)\n2. Verify git working directory clean (git status)\n3. Load codebase context (codebase-retrieval)\n4. Check relevant memories (list_memories -> read_memory)\n5. Identify all affected files and test files\n6. Make changes with full checklist\n7. Identify all files that import changed code\n8. Update all affected files\n9. Spawn verification agent (quality-engineer)\n10. Run comprehensive tests: `pytest [path] -v`\n11. Answer adversarial questions\n\n**STANDARD Execution**:\n1. Load context via codebase-retrieval\n2. Search downstream impacts (find_referencing_symbols OR grep)\n3. Make changes\n4. Run affected tests OR document manual verification\n5. Verify basic functionality\n\n**LIGHT Execution**:\n1. Quick scope check (files/lines within bounds)\n2. Make changes\n3. Quick sanity check (syntax valid, no obvious errors)\n4. Proceed with judgment\n\n**EXEMPT Execution**:\n1. Execute immediately\n2. No verification overhead\n\n### 4. Verification Phase\n\nRoute to appropriate verification based on tier and paths:\n\n| Compliance Tier | Verification Method | Token Cost | Timeout |\n|-----------------|---------------------|------------|---------|\n| STRICT | Sub-agent (quality-engineer) | 3-5K | 60s |\n| STANDARD | Direct test execution | 300-500 | 30s |\n| LIGHT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n| EXEMPT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n\n**Critical Path Override**: Paths matching `auth/`, `security/`, `crypto/`, `models/`, `migrations/` always trigger CRITICAL verification regardless of compliance tier.\n\n**Trivial Path Override**: Paths matching `*.md`, `docs/`, `*test*.py` may skip verification.\n\n### 4.5 Test Failure Escalation Protocol (TFEP)\n\n**CRITICAL**: When tests fail during the Verification Phase (Section 4), agents MUST follow this protocol. Ad-hoc fixes are PROHIBITED.\n\n#### TFEP Prohibition Rules (VIOLATION-level)\n\nThese rules apply to ALL compliance tiers that run tests (STRICT, STANDARD):\n\n1. **VIOLATION**: Agents MUST NOT fix any code in response to test failures without completing the TFEP workflow.\n2. **VIOLATION**: Agents MUST NOT modify test expectations to make failing tests pass without adversarial validation.\n3. **VIOLATION**: Ad-hoc patches derived from test output are PROHIBITED. The agent must not read a traceback and immediately edit code to resolve it.\n\n**Permitted Exceptions** (MAY fix directly without TFEP):\n- Single `ImportError`/`NameError` in test scaffolding the agent just wrote, affecting <=2 tests, where the error is in the test file itself (not in implementation code).\n- Lint/formatting failures (trivially fixable, unambiguous root cause).\n- Deprecation warnings (not failures).\n\n**Valid Adversarial Outcome**: \"Test expectations are wrong\" is a legitimate conclusion from adversarial debate. When the debate concludes that test expectations are outdated rather than the code being wrong, this is NOT grounds for the agent to directly edit the tests — it must be presented to the user for review.\n\n#### Test Baseline Snapshot (Pre-Implementation)\n\nBefore implementation begins, the agent MUST record a test baseline:\n\n1. Capture the list of all existing test files and test function names at task start (e.g., via `uv run pytest --collect-only -q` or directory listing).\n2. Store this baseline in memory for the duration of the task.\n3. On any test failure, classify each failing test as:\n   - **Pre-existing**: Test name appears in the baseline (existed before this task).\n   - **New**: Test name does NOT appear in the baseline (written by the agent during this task).\n4. This classification drives the MUST-escalate vs MAY-fix-directly decision below.\n\n#### Escalation Trigger Detection\n\n**MUST escalate (trigger TFEP):**\n- Any **pre-existing test** fails (tests in the baseline that were not modified by the agent). This is the primary trigger — regressions in existing tests indicate the implementation broke something.\n- **3 or more new tests** fail simultaneously (indicates a systemic issue, not a simple typo).\n- **Runtime exceptions in implementation code** (TypeError, AttributeError, KeyError, etc. in the code being tested, not in the test scaffolding itself).\n\n**Escalation gradient (within-TFEP, for future forensic integration):**\n- Repeated failure (same test cluster fails after fix attempt) → escalate from light to standard\n- Multi-file blast radius from recent changes → escalate\n- Low-confidence root cause from adversarial debate → escalate\n- Unresolved adversarial outcome (no winner/tie) → escalate\n- Second failed retest → escalate\n- Cross-domain or non-obvious regression → escalate\n\n#### TFEP Execution Flow\n\nWhen TFEP triggers, execute the following steps:\n\n**Step 1: Halt and freeze**\n1. **STOP** testing immediately.\n2. **FREEZE** implementation — no further code changes permitted.\n\n**Step 2: Construct failure context**\n3. Build a `failure_context` YAML package containing:\n   - `test_names`: list of failing test function names\n   - `test_files`: list of test files containing failures\n   - `error_output`: full traceback/error output\n   - `expected_behavior`: what was expected\n   - `actual_behavior`: what actually happened\n   - `changes_made`: files changed during this task with descriptions\n   - `task_description`: current task description\n   - `test_baseline`: the pre-implementation test baseline\n   - `escalation_count`: which TFEP trigger this is (1, 2, or 3)\n4. Write context to `{output_dir}/context.yaml`.\n\n**Step 3: Invoke forensic**\n5. Determine the forensic tier based on escalation count:\n   - 1st trigger → `--tier light --intent triage`\n   - 2nd trigger → `--tier standard`\n   - 3rd trigger → **FULL STOP**. Report to user. Do not attempt further fixes.\n6. Invoke: `/sc:forensic --tier {tier} --intent triage --caller task-unified --context {context_path} --output {output_dir} --depth quick`\n7. The forensic pipeline runs autonomously through all its phases and returns a structured return contract.\n\n**Step 4: Consume forensic results**\n8. Read the forensic return contract from `{output_dir}/return-contract.yaml`.\n9. Handle based on status:\n   - If `test_is_wrong == true`: Present to user for review. Do NOT auto-fix tests.\n   - If `status == \"success\"`: Proceed to Step 5 (tasklist insertion).\n   - If `status == \"partial\"` or `recommended_escalation != \"none\"`: Increment `escalation_count` and return to Step 3.\n   - If `status == \"failed\"`: Report to user, halt execution.\n\n**Step 5: Tasklist insertion**\n10. Read `tasklist_insertion_path` from the return contract.\n11. Insert the remediation block into the current tasklist:\n    - Add `## Failure Remediation Plan (Adjudicated)` heading.\n    - Insert remediation tasks BEFORE existing test/verification tasks.\n    - Preserve original tasklist structure — append, don't replace.\n\n**Step 6: Resume**\n12. Resume execution with `--compliance strict` starting from the inserted remediation tasks.\n13. After remediation tasks complete, re-run the original test suite.\n14. If tests pass: TFEP resolved successfully. Produce incident report and continue.\n15. If tests fail again: Increment `escalation_count`, return to Step 2.\n\n#### TFEP Incident Reporting\n\nAfter each TFEP resolution (success or escalation), produce `tfep-incident-report.md`:\n\n```markdown\n# TFEP Incident Report\n\n- **Trigger**: {which threshold rule fired}\n- **Escalation count**: {1, 2, or 3}\n- **Failing tests**: {test names and classification}\n- **Root cause**: {summary from rca-verdict.md}\n- **Solution**: {summary from solution-verdict.md}\n- **Outcome**: {success / escalated / failed}\n- **Forensic artifacts**: {path to output_dir}\n```\n\nThis report is committed to git alongside other forensic artifacts.\n\n#### Escalation Budget\n\n```\n1st TFEP trigger  → /sc:forensic --tier light --intent triage    (~5-8K tokens)\n2nd TFEP trigger  → /sc:forensic --tier standard                 (~15-20K tokens)\n3rd TFEP trigger  → FULL STOP. Report to user. Do not attempt further fixes.\n```\n\n### 5. Auto-loaded by pytest\n    40→│   ├── pm_agent/                  # Pre/post implementation patterns\n    41→│   │   ├── confidence.py          # Pre-execution confidence check\n    42→│   │   ├── self_check.py          # Post-implementation validation\n    43→│   │   ├── reflexion.py           # Error learning\n    44→│   │   └── token_budget.py        # Token allocation\n    45→│   ├── execution/                 # Parallel execution\n    46→│   │   ├── parallel.py            # Wave→Checkpoint→Wave\n    47→│   │   ├── reflection.py          # Meta-reasoning\n    48→│   │   └── self_correction.py     # Error recovery\n    49→│   └── cli/                       # Command-line interface\n    50→│       ├── main.py                # superclaude command\n    51→│       ├── doctor.py              # Health checks\n    52→│       └── install_skill.py       # Skill installation\n    53→│\n    54→├── Plugin Source (plugins/superclaude/)  # v5.0 - NOT ACTIVE YET\n    55→│   ├── agents/                    # Agent definitions\n    56→│   ├── commands/                  # Command definitions\n    57→│   ├── hooks/                     # Hook configurations\n    58→│   ├── scripts/                   # Shell scripts\n    59→│   └── skills/                    # Skill implementations\n    60→│\n    61→├── Tests (tests/)\n    62→│   ├── unit/                      # Component unit tests\n    63→│   └── integration/               # Plugin integration tests\n    64→│\n    65→└── Documentation (docs/)\n    66→    ├── architecture/              # Architecture decisions\n    67→    ├── developer-guide/           # Development guides\n    68→    ├── reference/                 # API reference\n    69→    ├── research/                  # Research findings\n    70→    └── user-guide/                # User documentation\n    71→```\n    72→\n    73→### **Future State (v5.0 - Planned)**\n    74→\n    75→- TypeScript plugin system (issue #419)\n    76→- Project-local `.claude-plugin/` detection\n    77→- Plugin marketplace distribution\n    78→- Enhanced MCP server integration\n    79→\n    80→---\n    81→\n    82→## ⚙️ **Design Principles**\n    83→\n    84→### **1. Evidence-Based Development**\n    85→\n    86→**Never guess** - always verify with official sources:\n    87→- Use Context7 MCP for official documentation\n    88→- Use WebFetch/WebSearch for research\n    89→- Check existing code with Glob/Grep before implementing\n    90→- Verify assumptions against test results\n    91→\n    92→**Anti-pattern**: Implementing based on assumptions or outdated knowledge\n    93→\n    94→### **2. Confidence-First Implementation**\n    95→\n    96→Check confidence BEFORE starting work:\n    97→- **≥90%**: Proceed with implementation\n    98→- **70-89%**: Present alternatives, continue investigation\n    99→- **<70%**: STOP - ask questions, investigate more\n   100→\n   101→**ROI**: Spend 100-200 tokens on confidence check to save 5,000-50,000 tokens on wrong direction\n   102→\n   103→### **3. Parallel-First Execution**\n   104→\n   105→Use **Wave → Checkpoint → Wave** pattern:\n   106→```\n   107→Wave 1: [Read file1, Read file2, Read file3] (parallel)\n   108→   ↓\n   109→Checkpoint: Analyze all files together\n   110→   ↓\n   111→Wave 2: [Edit file1, Edit file2, Edit file3] (parallel)\n   112→```\n   113→\n   114→**Benefit**: 3.5x faster than sequential execution\n   115→\n   116→**When to use**:\n   117→- Independent operations (reading multiple files)\n   118→- Batch transformations (editing multiple files)\n   119→- Parallel searches (grep across different directories)\n   120→\n   121→**When NOT to use**:\n   122→- Operations with dependencies (must wait for previous result)\n   123→- Sequential analysis (need to build context step-by-step)\n   124→\n   125→### **4. Token Efficiency**\n   126→\n   127→Allocate tokens based on task complexity:\n   128→- **Simple** (typo fix): 200 tokens\n   129→- **Medium** (bug fix): 1,000 tokens\n   130→- **Complex** (feature): 2,500 tokens\n   131→\n   132→**Confidence check ROI**: 25-250x token savings\n   133→\n   134→### **5. No Hallucinations**\n   135→\n   136→Use SelfCheckProtocol to prevent hallucinations:\n   137→\n   138→**The Four Questions**:\n   139→1. Are all tests passing? (show output)\n   140→2. Are all requirements met? (list items)\n   141→3. No assumptions without verification? (show docs)\n   142→4. Is there evidence? (test results, code changes, validation)\n   143→\n   144→**7 Red Flags**:\n   145→- \"Tests pass\" without output\n   146→- \"Everything works\" without evidence\n   147→- \"Implementation complete\" with failing tests\n   148→- Skipping error messages\n   149→- Ignoring warnings\n   150→- Hiding failures\n   151→- \"Probably works\" language\n   152→\n   153→---\n   154→\n   155→## 🚫 **Absolute Rules**\n   156→\n   157→### **Python Environment**\n   158→\n   159→1. **ALWAYS use UV** for Python operations:\n   160→   ```bash\n   161→   uv run pytest              # NOT: python -m pytest\n   162→   uv pip install package     # NOT: pip install package\n   163→   uv run python script.py    # NOT: python script.py\n   164→   ```\n   165→\n   166→2. **Package structure**: Use src/ layout\n   167→   - `src/superclaude/` for package code\n   168→   - `tests/` for test code\n   169→   - Never mix source and tests in same directory\n   170→\n   171→3. **Entry points**: Use pyproject.toml\n   172→   - CLI: `[project.scripts]`\n   173→   - Pytest plugin: `[project.entry-points.pytest11]`\n   174→\n   175→### **Testing**\n   176→\n   177→1. **All new features MUST have tests**\n   178→   - Unit tests for individual components\n   179→   - Integration tests for component interactions\n   180→   - Use pytest markers: `@pytest.mark.unit`, `@pytest.mark.integration`\n   181→\n   182→2. **Use PM Agent patterns in tests**:\n   183→   ```python\n   184→   @pytest.mark.confidence_check\n   185→   def test_feature(confidence_checker):\n   186→       context = {...}\n   187→       assert confidence_checker.assess(context) >= 0.7\n   188→\n   189→   @pytest.mark.self_check\n   190→   def test_implementation(self_check_protocol):\n   191→       passed, issues = self_check_protocol.validate(impl)\n   192→       assert passed\n   193→   ```\n   194→\n   195→3. **Test fixtures**: Use conftest.py for shared fixtures\n   196→\n   197→### **Git Workflow**\n   198→\n   199→1. **Branch structure**:\n   200→   - `master`: Production-ready code\n   201→   - `integration`: Testing ground (not yet created)\n   202→   - `feature/*`, `fix/*`, `docs/*`: Feature branches\n   203→\n   204→2. **Commit messages**: Use conventional commits\n   205→   - `feat:` - New feature\n   206→   - `fix:` - Bug fix\n   207→   - `docs:` - Documentation\n   208→   - `refactor:` - Code refactoring\n   209→   - `test:` - Adding tests\n   210→   - `chore:` - Maintenance\n   211→\n   212→3. **Never commit**:\n   213→   - `__pycache__/`, `*.pyc`\n   214→   - `.venv/`, `venv/`\n   215→   - Personal files (TODO.txt, CRUSH.md)\n   216→   - API keys, secrets\n   217→\n   218→### **Documentation**\n   219→\n   220→1. **Code documentation**:\n   221→   - All public functions need docstrings\n   222→   - Use type hints\n   223→   - Include usage examples in docstrings\n   224→\n   225→2. **Project documentation**:\n   226→   - Update CLAUDE.md for Claude Code guidance\n   227→   - Update README.md for user instructions\n   228→   - Update this PLANNING.md for architecture decisions\n   229→   - Update TASK.md for current work\n   230→   - Update KNOWLEDGE.md for insights\n   231→\n   232→3. **Keep docs synchronized**:\n   233→   - When code changes, update relevant docs\n   234→   - When features are added, update CHANGELOG.md\n   235→   - When architecture changes, update PLANNING.md\n   236→\n   237→### **Version Management**\n   238→\n   239→1. **Version sources of truth**:\n   240→   - Framework version: `VERSION` file (e.g., 4.2.0)\n   241→   - Python package version: `pyproject.toml` (e.g., 0.4.0)\n   242→   - NPM package version: `package.json` (should match VERSION)\n   243→\n   244→2. **When to bump versions**:\n   245→   - Major: Breaking API changes\n   246→   - Minor: New features, backward compatible\n   247→   - Patch: Bug fixes\n   248→\n   249→---\n   250→\n   251→## 🔄 **Development Workflow**\n   252→\n   253→### **Starting a New Feature**\n   254→\n   255→1. **Investigation Phase**:\n   256→   - Read PLANNING.md, TASK.md, KNOWLEDGE.md\n   257→   - Check for duplicates (Glob/Grep existing code)\n   258→   - Read official docs (Context7 MCP, WebFetch)\n   259→   - Search for OSS implementations (WebSearch)\n   260→   - Run confidence check (should be ≥90%)\n   261→\n   262→2. **Implementation Phase**:\n   263→   - Create feature branch: `git checkout -b feature/feature-name`\n   264→   - Write tests first (TDD)\n   265→   - Implement feature\n   266→   - Run tests: `uv run pytest`\n   267→   - Run linter: `make lint`\n   268→   - Format code: `make format`\n   269→\n   270→3. **Validation Phase**:\n   271→   - Run self-check protocol\n   272→   - Verify all tests passing\n   273→   - Check all requirements met\n   274→   - Confirm assumptions verified\n   275→   - Provide evidence\n   276→\n   277→4. **Documentation Phase**:\n   278→   - Update relevant documentation\n   279→   - Add docstrings\n   280→   - Update CHANGELOG.md\n   281→   - Update TASK.md (mark complete)\n   282→\n   283→5. **Review Phase**:\n   284→   - Create pull request\n   285→   - Request review\n   286→   - Address feedback\n   287→   - Merge to integration (or master if no integration branch)\n   288→\n   289→### **Fixing a Bug**\n   290→\n   291→1. **Root Cause Analysis**:\n   292→   - Reproduce the bug\n   293→   - Identify root cause (not symptoms)\n   294→   - Check reflexion memory for similar patterns\n   295→   - Run confidence check\n   296→\n   297→2. **Fix Implementation**:\n   298→   - Write failing test that reproduces bug\n   299→   - Implement fix\n   300→   - Verify test passes\n   301→   - Run full test suite\n   302→   - Record in reflexion memory\n   303→\n   304→3. **Prevention**:\n   305→   - Add regression test\n   306→   - Update documentation if needed\n   307→   - Share learnings in KNOWLEDGE.md\n   308→\n   309→---\n   310→\n   311→## 📊 **Quality Metrics**\n   312→\n   313→### **Code Quality**\n   314→\n   315→- **Test coverage**: Aim for >80%\n   316→- **Linting**: Zero ruff errors\n   317→- **Type checking**: Use type hints, minimal mypy errors\n   318→- **Documentation**: All public APIs documented\n   319→\n   320→### **PM Agent Metrics**\n   321→\n   322→- **Confidence check ROI**: 25-250x token savings\n   323→- **Self-check detection**: 94% hallucination detection rate\n   324→- **Parallel execution**: 3.5x speedup vs sequential\n   325→- **Token efficiency**: 30-50% reduction with proper budgeting\n   326→\n   327→### **Release Criteria**\n   328→\n   329→Before releasing a new version:\n   330→- ✅ All tests passing\n   331→- ✅ Documentation updated\n   332→- ✅ CHANGELOG.md updated\n   333→- ✅ Version numbers synced\n   334→- ✅ No known critical bugs\n   335→- ✅ Security audit passed (if applicable)\n   336→\n   337→---\n   338→\n   339→## 🔧 **Roadmap Generation Pipeline**\n   340→\n   341→### Pipeline Steps\n   342→\n   343→The `superclaude roadmap run` command executes a 9-step pipeline (8 stages,\n   344→with generate running as a parallel pair):\n   345→\n   346→| # | Step | Gate Tier | Timeout | Output File |\n   347→|---|------|-----------|---------|-------------|\n   348→| 1 | extract | STRICT | 300s | extraction.md |\n   349→| 2a | generate-{agent_a} | STRICT | 600s | roadmap-{agent_a}.md |\n   350→| 2b | generate-{agent_b} | STRICT | 600s | roadmap-{agent_b}.md |\n   351→| 3 | diff | STANDARD | 300s | diff-analysis.md |\n   352→| 4 | debate | STRICT | 600s | debate-transcript.md |\n   353→| 5 | score | STANDARD | 300s | base-selection.md |\n   354→| 6 | merge | STRICT | 600s | roadmap.md |\n   355→| 7 | test-strategy | STANDARD | 300s | test-strategy.md |\n   356→| 8 | spec-fidelity | STRICT | 600s | spec-fidelity.md |\n   357→\n   358→Steps 2a and 2b run in parallel.\n   359→\n   360→### Gate Ordering\n   361→\n   362→```\n   363→extract → generate (parallel) → diff → debate → score → merge → test-strategy → spec-fidelity\n   364→```\n   365→\n   366→### --no-validate Behavior\n   367→\n   368→The `--no-validate` flag skips only the **post-pipeline validation** subsystem\n   369→(the `superclaude roadmap validate` command auto-invocation). It does NOT skip\n   370→the spec-fidelity pipeline step. The spec-fidelity step always runs as part of\n   371→the core pipeline.\n   372→\n   373→### --retrospective Flag\n   374→\n   375→The `--retrospective <file>` flag loads a retrospective markdown file and\n   376→injects its content into the extraction prompt as advisory \"areas to watch\"\n   377→context. If the file is missing, extraction proceeds normally without error.\n   378→\n   379→### Post-Pipeline Validation\n   380→\n   381→After pipeline completion (unless `--no-validate`), the system   71→    rollout_mode: Literal[\"shadow\", \"soft\", \"full\"] = \"shadow\"\n    72→\n    73→\n    74→def load_whitelist(\n    75→    path: Path | None,\n    76→    rollout_mode: Literal[\"shadow\",    - full: critical + major unsuppressed\n        \"\"\"\n        effective_mode = mode or self.rollout_mode\n        unsuppressed = self.unsuppressed_findings\n\n        if effective_mode == \"shadow\":\n            return 0\n        elif effective_mode == \"soft\":\n            return sum(1 for f in unsuppressed if f.severity == \"critical\")\n        else:  # full\n            return
